Post_ID: 2767863214936816650	|Post_Code: CZpbO3hLfwK	|Owner_ID: 22580829951	|Likes: 9	|Time_Stamp: 1644175029	|Tags: ['#Mournes', '#Mournes', '#LeaveNoTrace', '#mountains', '#outdoors', '#walking', '#hiking', '#leavenotrace']	|Caption: Graffiti in the #Mournes <br>This picture is of a handrail we replaced last year at a gateway to the Trassey valley. As well as having rotted away, the previous support was covered in graffiti, apparently documenting dates a particular couple visited. The same has occurred on the new rail despite previous etchings having been sanded off. The occurrence is not isolated to this location and the same initials (and occasionally the apparently corresponding names, Glen and Elaine) have appeared on stiles, way markers and other surfaces throughout the #Mournes. We are pleased to note that graffiti is not a particular issue in the area, but it would be sad if it became the case. As well as creating work for our small team who maintain the visitor infrastructure, feedback from other visitors is overwhelmingly clear that this - and other memorials/ markings â€“ intrude significantly on the experience of enjoying an unspoiled landscape. We appreciate that the practice is motivated for this couple by a love of the Mournes as well as each other but would suggest that appreciation of the place is best observed by a #LeaveNoTrace approach. Perhaps photographs and a diary for recording the other love? If you happen to see this Elaine and Glen, we wish you every happiness and ask that you enjoy future visits to the Mournes without visibly marking them. #mountains #outdoors #walking #hiking #leavenotrace

A common strategy is to hike down from the plateau and cache water at designated camps before cycling. I did this for two campsites (two separate round trip hikes for each campsite) which gives an awesome perspective of the riding to come. Short, chilly days and long cold nights are another challenge to contend with in the winter, but the total absence of crowds is the reward for braving the low temps, I had the entire place to myself to freeze my ass off alone for three days. <br><br>Regardless of the direction chosen, the loop starts by dropping â€œintoâ€ the rim zone and finishes with a climb back â€œoutâ€, and one really does have the impression of entering into another realm, separated from the world above. You become (or should become) very aware of your gear, essentially your life-support, your water supply, your level of energy or fatigue, the distances separating you from camp, from water, from warmth, from safety. It is one of those all-to-rare places where you really feel like you are on a dynamic and indifferent planet, our own, not a sanitized, secured terrarium for Homo Sapiens. <br>(continued on next post...)<br>#bikepacking #bikepackingbags,  #ursusbikepacks, #faitenfrance, #artisansducycle, #konaexplosif, #Kona, #whiterimtrail, #canyonlands, #canyonlandsnationalpark, #canyonlandsnps, #leavenotrace, #utah, #moab

Post_ID: 2767121571819685661	|Post_Code: CZmymiiogcd	|Owner_ID: 45464644251	|Likes: 31	|Time_Stamp: 1644086618	|Tags: ['#bikepacking', '#bikepackingbags', '#ursusbikepacks', '#faitenfrance', '#artisansducycle', '#konaexplosif', '#Kona', '#whiterimtrail', '#canyonlands', '#canyonlandsnationalpark', '#canyonlandsnps', '#leavenotrace', '#utah', '#moab']	|Caption: Any cycling trip can elevate even a relatively mundane or familiar area to the realm of adventure, awakening or reawakening a deeper connection to, relationship with and appreciation for that land.  Bikepacking through one of the most spectacular landscapes imaginable, and those days in the saddle and nights in the tent can quickly become some of the most transcendent experiences one can have, a voyage that simply cannot be reduced to the metrics of maps and distances, one that takes place in you soul. <br><br>The â€œWhite Rimâ€ (Canyonlands National Park, Utah) had been on my radar for a few years, as something I could do during one of my trips back to the US, usually in the winter to avoid the Las Vegas heat.  No wide angle lenses, HD screen, no poetry or prose can ever really capture what being immersed in such an environment is like. Nevertheless, I humbly offer my trip report and a few photos. <br><br>The route is only about 160km long, the riding is never very technical, and it is often ridden in a day by people much fitter or hurried than myself. I opted for two nights under that black sidereal canopy, a more leisurely pace leaving time for wandering, wonder, and contemplation.<br> <br>Vehicle access is via a vast plateau forming a kind of elevated peninsula stretching southward into the triangular confluence of the Green and Colorado rivers. This plateau is delimited by sheer bluffs with only a handful of roads and trails descending 400m down to the White Rim. From there, the route follows the characteristically whiteish, crumbling rim of even deeper chasms eroded away by the Green and the Colorado, which are only rarely visible along the route, mostly hidden by their own incisions that they've dug into the older, deeper layers of rock. <br><br>(continued on next post...)<br>#bikepacking #bikepackingbags,  #ursusbikepacks, #faitenfrance, #artisansducycle, #konaexplosif, #Kona, #whiterimtrail, #canyonlands, #canyonlandsnationalpark, #canyonlandsnps, #leavenotrace, #utah, #moab
